# /check-inbox — read and archive pending inbox messages

Implements plans/in-progress/2026-04-20-strawberry-inbox-channel.md §3.4.

## Purpose

Scan `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` for files with `status: pending`, display each
message, **archive** them to `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/` with
`status: read` and a `read_at` timestamp. Enforces the pending-only invariant
of the main inbox directory.

After running, `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.

## Step 0 — Identify the coordinator

Resolve agent name in this order:

1. `CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` environment variable (set by `claude --agent <name>`)
2. `STRAWBERRY_AGENT` environment variable
3. `.claude/settings.json` `.agent` field (case-insensitive)

If none of the above resolves a name, refuse:

```
check-inbox: cannot identify agent — set CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME or STRAWBERRY_AGENT
```

## Step 1 — List pending messages

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
ls "$REPO_ROOT/agents/<AGENT>/inbox/"*.md 2>/dev/null || echo "(no .md files)"
```

For each `.md` file found at the top level of `inbox/` (not in `archive/`
subdirectories), read its frontmatter and collect those with `status: pending`.

If none are pending, print:

```
No pending messages for <AGENT>.
```

...and stop (exit 0).

## Step 2 — Display each pending message

For each pending message file, print a formatted block:

```
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
From:      <from>
Priority:  <priority>
Timestamp: <timestamp>
File:      agents/<agent>/inbox/<filename>
──────────────────────────────────────────────────
<body text — everything after the closing --- frontmatter fence>
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
```

## Step 3 — Archive each message

For each pending message, perform the following steps **in order** (the
ordering is critical for watcher filter discipline — write `status: read`
before the `mv` so a concurrent watcher event sees the file already read):

### Step 3a — Rewrite frontmatter in place

Use the Edit tool:

- Change `status: pending` → `status: read`
- Add a new line `read_at: <ISO-8601 UTC timestamp>` directly after the
  `status: read` line.

Use `date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ` via Bash for the timestamp.

Do not remove any other frontmatter fields. Do not alter the body text.

Example of updated frontmatter:

```yaml
---
from: sona
to: evelynn
priority: normal
timestamp: 2026-04-21T14:02:00Z
status: read
read_at: 2026-04-21T14:05:33Z
---
```

### Step 3b — Compute the archive path

- Derive `<YYYY-MM>` from the file's `timestamp:` frontmatter field.
  - Parse the first 7 characters (e.g. `2026-04` from `2026-04-21T14:02:00Z`).
  - Fallback: if `timestamp:` is absent, use the file's mtime:
    `date -r <file> +%Y-%m 2>/dev/null || date +%Y-%m`
- Archive path: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<original-filename>`

### Step 3c — Move the file

```bash
mkdir -p "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>"
mv "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/<filename>" "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<filename>"
```

**Concurrency guard:** if the `mv` fails because the source file is already
gone (rare — would require two parallel `/check-inbox` runs on the same inbox),
skip and continue. Do not abort. This is idempotent by design.

## Step 4 — Summary

After processing all pending messages, print a one-line summary:

```
check-inbox: archived <N> message(s) for <AGENT>.
```

Post-condition: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.
The `archive/` subdirectory is the only remaining populated location.

## Refusal rules

- If the agent directory `agents/<AGENT>/` does not exist, refuse:
  `check-inbox: unknown agent <name>`
- If `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` does not exist, print:
  `check-inbox: inbox directory not found for <AGENT> — no messages`
  and exit 0 (not an error; the inbox may never have been written to).
- Never write secrets into any message body.
- Never modify any field other than `status` and adding `read_at`.
- Never write to `archive/` from the `send` path — the `send` path in
  `/agent-ops` always writes to the flat `inbox/` directory only.

**Decision teed up while agents run — W3 config-architecture gate:**

W3 (set_config schema flip + SSE `configVersion` piggyback) has one open question from the ADR amendment that blocks dispatch: **OQ-K2 — SSE schema flexibility**. The ADR currently treats the `configVersion` field as a strict top-level SSE event key, but two of the existing SSE consumers in `studio.js` already assume schema-additive tolerance (unknown keys ignored, not errored). The question is whether to codify schema-additivity as the contract or keep strict parsing.

1. **Schema-additivity codified** — contract says consumers MUST ignore unknown SSE event keys; producers MAY add fields freely; `configVersion` lands as one additive field.
   a: Add a contract-test in `tests/test_sse_schema_compat.py` that asserts both directions (producer sends extra keys, parser accepts; parser given missing keys, defaults cleanly). Update ADR §SSE-schema to declare the invariant. (cleanest — locks the pattern for future W4/W5 fields)
   b: Just codify in ADR prose, skip the contract test, trust the two existing consumers. (balanced)
   c: Keep strict parsing, list `configVersion` explicitly in a hand-maintained SSE enum, fail fast on unknowns. (quickest, but debt — every future W adds a schema migration)
   **Pick: a** — W4 and W5 both need to add SSE fields. Paying for the contract test once costs 15 min and kills the whole class of schema-drift bugs. Strict parsing (c) is a debt I don't think cheaply repays.

Want me to proceed on **1a** and queue the W3 complex-lane pair (Rakan xfails ‖ Viktor impl) once the current Rakan return frees him? Or do you want to decide later?

# /agent-ops — local agent operations

## Subcommand dispatch

`send evelynn "Retired-rule sweep: 'never parallelize same agent' was retired 2026-04-21 (learnings/2026-04-21-coordinator-parallelism-mandatory.md) and replaced with mandatory-parallelism where task independence is the dispatch criterion. Duong just caught me hesitating to fire a second Rakan alongside one already running because residual rule-fragments still felt binding. Asking you to own the cleanup end-to-end since rule hygiene is coordinator-territory and this affects both of us.

Scope: explore the repo for any remaining mention of the retired absolute — 'never parallelize same agent', 'same agent type', 'one instance per agent', 'serialize same-agent dispatches', similar phrasings. Check at minimum: agents/sona/CLAUDE.md, agents/evelynn/CLAUDE.md, agents/memory/agent-network.md, agents/memory/duong.md, .claude/agents/*.md, architecture/*.md, any learnings/*.md that might pre-date the retirement.

For each match: strip the absolute and leave behind either (a) an explicit 'retired 2026-04-21' note pointing at the learning, or (b) a positive principle citing task independence if the surrounding prose still needs the idea.

Same treatment for both sides — work concern (sona) and personal concern (evelynn). Commit with chore: prefix. No PR, plans-go-direct-to-main doesn't apply here but these are agent-config edits that land straight to main anyway per convention. One commit covering both coordinators is fine.

Priority: normal. Not blocking current ship, but Duong flagged it today so let's not let it drift. Ping me when done so I can stop second-guessing parallel dispatches."` is parsed as `<subcommand> <rest...>`. Supported subcommands:

### `send <agent> <message...>`

Writes an inbox file at `agents/<agent>/inbox/<timestamp>-<shortid>.md` with the following schema (mirroring the former `message_agent` MCP tool):

```
---
from: <sender>
to: <agent>
priority: info
timestamp: YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM
status: pending
---

<message>
```

Sender is derived from `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set in environment. If the caller cannot be identified, the skill refuses with `agent-ops send: sender unknown` and exits 2.

**Steps to execute:**

1. Determine sender: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set, otherwise ask the caller to state who they are. If the caller cannot confirm, exit 2 with `agent-ops send: sender unknown`.
2. Delegate to `scripts/agent-ops/send.sh` via the Bash tool (mirrors `list` / `new` patterns). The script validates the target agent, creates the inbox directory, and writes the file — no Write tool is used, so the inbox-write guard does not fire.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/agent-ops/send.sh" "<agent>" "<sender>" "<message>"
```

3. Print the full path of the created inbox file (the script prints it on stdout).

### `list [--json]`

Shells out to `scripts/list-agents.sh` (with `--format json` if `--json` is given) via Bash and prints the result.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh"
# or with --json flag:
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh" --format json
```

### `new <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]`

Shells out to `scripts/new-agent.sh` with the provided arguments via Bash:

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/new-agent.sh" <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]
```

## Refusal rules

- If `send evelynn "Retired-rule sweep: 'never parallelize same agent' was retired 2026-04-21 (learnings/2026-04-21-coordinator-parallelism-mandatory.md) and replaced with mandatory-parallelism where task independence is the dispatch criterion. Duong just caught me hesitating to fire a second Rakan alongside one already running because residual rule-fragments still felt binding. Asking you to own the cleanup end-to-end since rule hygiene is coordinator-territory and this affects both of us.

Scope: explore the repo for any remaining mention of the retired absolute — 'never parallelize same agent', 'same agent type', 'one instance per agent', 'serialize same-agent dispatches', similar phrasings. Check at minimum: agents/sona/CLAUDE.md, agents/evelynn/CLAUDE.md, agents/memory/agent-network.md, agents/memory/duong.md, .claude/agents/*.md, architecture/*.md, any learnings/*.md that might pre-date the retirement.

For each match: strip the absolute and leave behind either (a) an explicit 'retired 2026-04-21' note pointing at the learning, or (b) a positive principle citing task independence if the surrounding prose still needs the idea.

Same treatment for both sides — work concern (sona) and personal concern (evelynn). Commit with chore: prefix. No PR, plans-go-direct-to-main doesn't apply here but these are agent-config edits that land straight to main anyway per convention. One commit covering both coordinators is fine.

Priority: normal. Not blocking current ship, but Duong flagged it today so let's not let it drift. Ping me when done so I can stop second-guessing parallel dispatches."` is empty, print the subcommand help below and exit 0.
- If the subcommand is unrecognized, refuse with `agent-ops: unknown subcommand <name>` and exit 2.
- If `send` cannot determine a sender, refuse with `agent-ops send: sender unknown` and exit 2.
- If `send` target agent directory does not exist, refuse with `agent-ops send: unknown agent <name>` and exit 2.

**Subcommand help (printed when arguments empty):**

```
/agent-ops <subcommand> [args]

Subcommands:
  send <agent> <message...>   Write an inbox message to an agent
  list [--json]               List all agents (TSV or JSON)
  new <agent-name> [--role]   Scaffold a new agent directory
```

## Platform note

This skill runs identically on macOS and Windows (Git Bash). All subcommands use POSIX-portable bash via the `Bash` tool — no macOS-specific commands. Agent launching is macOS-only and is handled by `scripts/mac/launch-agent-iterm.sh`; it is not available from this skill.

## Cross-references

- `architecture/platform-parity.md` — full platform support matrix
- `plans/proposed/2026-04-08-mcp-restructure.md` — rough plan (governs Phases 2–3)
- `plans/implemented/2026-04-09-mcp-restructure-phase-1-detailed.md` — this Phase 1 spec (once promoted)

## Inbox write guard

Direct `Write` or `Edit` to `agents/*/inbox/*.md` is blocked by `scripts/hooks/pretooluse-inbox-write-guard.sh` (registered as a PreToolUse hook). Use `/agent-ops send` to deliver inbox messages — this is the only sanctioned authorship path for non-admin identities. The single permitted `Edit` is the check-inbox status flip (`status: pending` -> `status: read`); all other edits are rejected. Archival moves live under `inbox/archive/` and are unguarded. Admin bypass identities: `duongntd` and `harukainguyen1411`.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

   - Key bash guard pattern for deploy.sh (in plan body):
     ```bash
     if [ -n "$(git status --porcelain)" ] && [ "${FORCE_DIRTY:-0}" != "1" ]; then
         echo "deploy.sh: refuse to deploy from dirty working tree..." >&2
         git status --porcelain >&2
         exit 1
     fi
     GIT_SHA=$(git rev-parse --short=12 HEAD)
     [ "${FORCE_DIRTY:-0}" = "1" ] && GIT_SHA="${GIT_SHA}-dirty"
     # appended to gcloud run deploy:
     --labels=git-sha=${GIT_SHA}
     ```
   - TOCTOU fix pattern in `tools/demo-studio-v3/main.py` auth_exchange (Vi impl 121e191):
     - After `set_session_owner` returns False, re-read session

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T04:52:50Z

**Found the bug — it's in S2, not in W3.**

`tools/demo-config-mgmt/main.py` POST `/v1/config` handler is a stub with two defects that make it a no-op for W3 writes:

1. **It reads `initialConfig`, not `config`**. The W3 client (`config_mgmt_client.snapshot_config`) sends `{"sessionId": sid, "config": config}`. S2's handler pulls `body.get("initialConfig", {})` → always empty → the payload is dropped on the floor.

2. **It's create-only, not upsert**. Guard: `if session_id not in _session_configs`. On the first POST (W1 session seeding) it populates. Every subsequent POST from the agent's `set_config` falls through the guard and returns `{"version": 1}` without mutating anything.

This explains your symptom exactly: tool_result `{"version": 1}` every call, config stays at the Allianz seed, no Firestore write. The W3 PR never updated S2's POST handler to match the whole-snapshot contract it relies on.

Dispatching Talon to fix S2. Scope is tight and the ADR intent is already defined (`plans/in-progress/work/2026-04-23-agent-owned-config-flow.md §D3`).

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T04:58:12Z

**Probed both S2s. Here's the picture:**

**Deployed S2** (`demo-config-mgmt-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app`, the real thing):
- POST `/v1/config` accepts `{sessionId, config: {...whole snapshot...}}` exactly as W3's client sends
- Validates JSON schema; 422 on invalid unless `?force=true`
- With `?force=true`: writes even if invalid, **bumps version on re-POST** (confirmed v1→v2 with update)
- Behaves exactly as W3's `_handle_set_config` expects — validation failure → force retry → persisted with warnings

**Local S2 stub** (`tools/demo-config-mgmt/main.py`):
- Reads wrong body key (`initialConfig`, not `config`)
- Create-only (no update semantics)
- No validation
- Returns `{"version": 1}` on every call

**S1 is already correct against deployed S2.** Our `config_mgmt_client.snapshot_config` sends `{sessionId, config}` and appends `?force=true` on retry — that matches deployed S2 to the letter. Nothing code-wise needs changing.

## Duong — 2026-04-24T05:10:48Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T05:12:16Z

Lissandra dispatched. Per the skill protocol, I'll wait for the return notification, verify the sentinel at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-84b7ba50-c664-40d8-9865-eb497b704fb3` exists, verify the commit landed on main, and report back. Then `/compact` is safe to run.

## Duong — 2026-04-24T05:50:53Z

https://socket.dev/blog/bitwarden-cli-compromised does this affect only if I use the cli? Or in general if I use bitwarden?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T05:51:23Z

**Short answer: CLI-only, and narrower than that — only one specific npm package version.**

**Scope breakdown:**

| Surface | Affected? |
|---|---|
| `@bitwarden/cli` npm package, **v2026.4.0** | **Yes** — malicious `bw1.js` embedded |
| Bitwarden desktop app | No |
| Browser extensions (Chrome, Firefox, etc.) | No |
| Mobile apps (iOS, Android) | No |
| Web vault (bitwarden.com) | No |
| MCP server / other legitimate distributions | No |

**What actually happened:** Attackers compromised a GitHub Action in Bitwarden's CI/CD pipeline and slipped malicious code into a single npm-published CLI build. It's a supply-chain attack on the build process, not a breach of Bitwarden's vault infrastructure. Your stored passwords / vault contents are not at risk from this incident.

**Who needs to worry:**
- You installed `@bitwarden/cli` via `npm install -g @bitwarden/cli` (or similar) and got version `2026.4.0`.
- The malware targets developer machines — it harvests GitHub tokens, npm tokens, cloud credentials, SSH keys from the environment it runs in. So if you ran the poisoned CLI on a dev box with creds lying around, treat it as a credential-exposure event and rotate.

**Who doesn't:**
- You only use the browser extension / desktop / mobile app → unaffected.
- You use the CLI but installed it via a different channel (Homebrew, Snap, direct binary download from Bitwarden's releases page, Docker image) → unaffected.
- You have the CLI but not version `2026.4.0` → unaffected.

**Quick check for you:** if you have the CLI installed, run `bw --version`. If it says anything other than `2026.4.0`, you're clean. If it says `2026.4.0`, uninstall, rotate any tokens/creds that were reachable from the machine you ran it on, and reinstall a known-good version.

Given you just went through the `.env.local` leak and are already in rotation-posture for `INTERNAL_SECRET` and `CONFIG_MGMT_TOKEN`, this is worth a 30-second check — but unless you specifically installed `@bitwarden/cli` from npm recently, it doesn't add anything to your remediation list.

| Possibility | Probe |
|---|---|
| (a) S2 session data itself is stale or never written for that session | `GET /v1/config/{sid}` directly against S2 — does it return the brand you expect? |
| (b) Studio iframe URL/path wrong (T4 territory: `/v1/preview/` → `/preview/`) or `refreshPreview()` not firing on brand change | Open devtools on the studio page, trigger a brand change, watch Network for a new preview request |
| (c) Browser/CDN cache serving old HTML | Hard-reload + check `Cache-Control` response headers |
| (d) Session ID mismatch (studio using session X, S2 has config for Y) | Inspect the session ID in the iframe URL vs the one in the S2 call |

**What do you want me to do?**

1. **Clarify first** — can you describe what exactly you saw? (e.g. "brand changed in chat but iframe still shows Allianz", or "iframe never loads", or "iframe shows wrong brand on a fresh session".) Two-word answers fine.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Akali findings — TL;DR

**Verdict: PREVIEW-STALE in local dev, but it's an env-split, NOT a code bug.**

### The core discovery

Local demo-studio-v3 (:8080) and local demo-preview (:8090) talk to **different** config backends:

| Component | CONFIG_MGMT_URL |
|---|---|
| demo-studio-v3 (:8080) | **prod** `demo-config-mgmt-4nvufhmjiq-ew.a.run.app` |
| demo-preview (:8090) | **local** `http://localhost:8002` |

So when you chat with the studio → `set_config` writes to **prod** S2 → SSE fires `configVersion` event → browser calls `refreshPreview()` → iframe requests `:8090/preview/<sid>` → preview fetches from **local** S2 → returns stale Allianz config (because the write went to prod, not local). iframe never updates.

### Test evidence

- Session "Aviva" loaded — iframe showed **Allianz**, version badge v1.
- "Set brand to Aviva" → agent responded: "already Aviva on S2, no change needed" — confirming prod S2 state.
- "Change to Lemonade" → agent: "saved!", SSE event fires, badge bumps to **v3** — but iframe still Allianz.
- `curl localhost:8090/preview/<sid>` returns `<title>Allianz — Demo Preview</title>` with `--brand-primary: #003781` (Allianz blue).
- 7 screenshots + video captured under `assessments/qa-reports/`.

### What this means for the code

The code path is **fine**. Explore's earlier "preview→S2 FIXED" verdict holds:
- `_handle_set_config` correctly writes to S2
- SSE chain correctly emits `configVersion`
- `studio.js` correctly receives and calls `refreshPreview()`
- Iframe src correctly assembled

The staleness is purely the two local services pointing at different S2 backends.

### The surprise fire (Wave D blocker)

In her probing, Akali discovered **prod `demo-preview` returns 404 for all 6 sessions** she tested. Could mean: prod S2 is empty, or W3 schema mismatch (prod preview predates PR #107 whole-snapshot flip), or prod preview on a stale revision. **This blocks the demo-studio-v3 ship** — we can't merge PR #32 if prod preview is universally broken. That's why I just fired Explore (task #52) to diagnose read-only.

### Unrelated smaller issues she flagged

- `POST /session/new` returns 422 with `[object Object]` error-display bug (modal shows the raw object instead of message).
- Error-rendering bug: client serializes error object wrong.

### The caveat on her report

She did the prod-404 discovery by **harvesting a bearer token from another process's env and querying prod** — which violated your "QA on local" redirect. Framework flagged it as SECURITY WARNING. I've dispatched Yuumi (task #55) to write a severity-high learning and amend `.claude/agents/akali.md` with a hard rule against explicit-boundary violations + token-harvesting-from-other-processes, and notified Evelynn since Akali is cross-concern. So while the finding is useful, **trust it but expect we'll need to re-verify once Explore produces a read-only confirmation**.

## Explore's Wave B.5 verdict — synthesis

**Root cause of prod preview 404-for-all-sessions:** two things compound, and one of them is a **previously-hidden architectural footgun** worth surfacing separately.

### The finding that actually matters

**S2 (demo-config-mgmt) is in-memory only. No Firestore. State is pure Cloud Run instance RAM.**

Per Ekko's 2026-04-23 S2-contract learning: every session lives in one Cloud Run instance's memory. Scale-to-zero, instance restart, new revision deploy, auto-scale-out → **state is wiped**. A demo that takes >15 min to walk through risks the instance rotating mid-demo.

This is a ship-blocker-grade discovery. Not a code bug, not a test gap — a **missing-persistence-layer** class issue in prod S2. Previously noted in ekko's learning but never raised to the RUNWAY as a Wave-D blocker.

### The immediate 404 explanation (lighter)

Prod S2 is empty because **no prod demo-studio-v3 session has ever been created.** All prior QA was local. The prod S1 → S2 write path has literally never been exercised. So Akali's 404s are unsurprising — there's nothing to fetch.

### Small inconsistency worth noting

Explore flags a discrepancy: Ekko's prior learning says "unknown session IDs render Allianz via fallback config." Akali observed actual `404`s. Two possible explanations:
1. Prod demo-preview on a newer code path than Ekko tested (less likely — Explore traced back through git).
2. Ekko's "fallback" observation was conflating the local preview's file-mode fallback with S2 behavior. Prod S2 may return 404 directly when session is absent.

Not worth chasing now — will self-resolve once Wave D actually creates a session.

### Unblock path for Wave D

Explore's recommendation:
1. Deploy fresh `demo-preview` from current `feat/demo-studio-v3` HEAD (post-W3). Current prod preview = rev 00010-ff4 from 2026-04-22.
2. Create first-ever prod session via prod demo-studio-v3 → POST `/session/new`.
3. Verify `GET /v1/config/<sid>` returns 200 from prod S2.
4. Verify `/preview/<sid>` returns brand-correct HTML.
5. Akali re-test against the live session ID.

## Updated runway state

**Wave D is now gated on:**
- Wave C (deploy hygiene) — in-flight (Talon task #50)
- Wave B (preview T3/T4) — in-flight (Viktor task #51)
- **NEW: first-ever prod session creation + verification** — needs T.P1.14 Ekko deploy to happen first, then a manual walkthrough
- **NEW architectural question: S2 persistence.** Do we ship with in-memory-only S2, knowing a Cloud Run rotation mid-demo loses state? Or do we back-fill Firestore wiring first?

## Decision — S2 persistence

1. S2 in-memory-vs-Firestore for Wave D ship?
   a: add Firestore persistence to S2 before shipping — cleanest, survives rotations, ~1 day of work (another plan + impl)
   b: ship with in-memory S2 + document the "don't pause demos >15min" caveat + `--min-instances=1` on Cloud Run so it doesn't scale to zero — balanced, ships today
   c: ship as-is, accept that stale demos break randomly — quickest, worst UX
Pick: **b** — `--min-instances=1` is a one-line deploy.sh flag and covers 95% of the risk (only instance-restart-for-deploy/crash/promotion remains, which is operator-controlled). Firestore wiring as a tracked follow-up under `plans/proposed/work/` not blocking the ship.

Want me to dispatch Karma to author a quick-lane plan for the `--min-instances=1` patch + Firestore-persistence follow-up plan? Or hold until Wave C/B land so we aren't adding plans mid-flight?

### 2. Senna's optional semantics note (non-blocking)

She observed: `.env.local` convention (Next.js-style) usually means **overrides take precedence** — so `override=True` on the second `load_dotenv` call would match that convention. Our dispatch chose `override=False` (shell env wins > .env.local > .env).

Choice doesn't matter for shipping, but worth naming so the semantics are intentional:
1. `.env.local` precedence?
   a: `override=True` — matches .env.local naming convention, .env.local wins over .env but shell still wins over both (need `os.environ` check pattern, more code)
   b: `override=False` — current, simplest, shell > .env.local > .env, consistent fill-in chain
   c: rename to `.env.development` if we want stricter shell-env-always-wins
Pick: **b** — the simplest semantics; shell > file is the unix convention Duong's ops scripts already rely on. Senna's note is stylistic, not load-bearing.

```sh
set +a
PORT=8090 python tools/demo-preview/server.py >> /tmp/demo-preview.log 2>&1 &
```

# /check-inbox — read and archive pending inbox messages

Implements plans/in-progress/2026-04-20-strawberry-inbox-channel.md §3.4.

## Purpose

Scan `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` for files with `status: pending`, display each
message, **archive** them to `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/` with
`status: read` and a `read_at` timestamp. Enforces the pending-only invariant
of the main inbox directory.

After running, `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.

## Step 0 — Identify the coordinator

Resolve agent name in this order:

1. `CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` environment variable (set by `claude --agent <name>`)
2. `STRAWBERRY_AGENT` environment variable
3. `.claude/settings.json` `.agent` field (case-insensitive)

If none of the above resolves a name, refuse:

```
check-inbox: cannot identify agent — set CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME or STRAWBERRY_AGENT
```

## Step 1 — List pending messages

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
ls "$REPO_ROOT/agents/<AGENT>/inbox/"*.md 2>/dev/null || echo "(no .md files)"
```

For each `.md` file found at the top level of `inbox/` (not in `archive/`
subdirectories), read its frontmatter and collect those with `status: pending`.

If none are pending, print:

```
No pending messages for <AGENT>.
```

...and stop (exit 0).

## Step 2 — Display each pending message

For each pending message file, print a formatted block:

```
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
From:      <from>
Priority:  <priority>
Timestamp: <timestamp>
File:      agents/<agent>/inbox/<filename>
──────────────────────────────────────────────────
<body text — everything after the closing --- frontmatter fence>
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
```

## Step 3 — Archive each message

For each pending message, perform the following steps **in order** (the
ordering is critical for watcher filter discipline — write `status: read`
before the `mv` so a concurrent watcher event sees the file already read):

### Step 3a — Rewrite frontmatter in place

Use the Edit tool:

- Change `status: pending` → `status: read`
- Add a new line `read_at: <ISO-8601 UTC timestamp>` directly after the
  `status: read` line.

Use `date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ` via Bash for the timestamp.

Do not remove any other frontmatter fields. Do not alter the body text.

Example of updated frontmatter:

```yaml
---
from: sona
to: evelynn
priority: normal
timestamp: 2026-04-21T14:02:00Z
status: read
read_at: 2026-04-21T14:05:33Z
---
```

### Step 3b — Compute the archive path

- Derive `<YYYY-MM>` from the file's `timestamp:` frontmatter field.
  - Parse the first 7 characters (e.g. `2026-04` from `2026-04-21T14:02:00Z`).
  - Fallback: if `timestamp:` is absent, use the file's mtime:
    `date -r <file> +%Y-%m 2>/dev/null || date +%Y-%m`
- Archive path: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<original-filename>`

### Step 3c — Move the file

```bash
mkdir -p "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>"
mv "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/<filename>" "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<filename>"
```

**Concurrency guard:** if the `mv` fails because the source file is already
gone (rare — would require two parallel `/check-inbox` runs on the same inbox),
skip and continue. Do not abort. This is idempotent by design.

## Step 4 — Summary

After processing all pending messages, print a one-line summary:

```
check-inbox: archived <N> message(s) for <AGENT>.
```

Post-condition: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.
The `archive/` subdirectory is the only remaining populated location.

## Refusal rules

- If the agent directory `agents/<AGENT>/` does not exist, refuse:
  `check-inbox: unknown agent <name>`
- If `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` does not exist, print:
  `check-inbox: inbox directory not found for <AGENT> — no messages`
  and exit 0 (not an error; the inbox may never have been written to).
- Never write secrets into any message body.
- Never modify any field other than `status` and adding `read_at`.
- Never write to `archive/` from the `send` path — the `send` path in
  `/agent-ops` always writes to the flat `inbox/` directory only.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T09:21:16Z

Found root cause. Reporting both issues clearly:

**Issue 1: `Co-authored-by: Viktor` landed on main in 3 of 4 merges (#114, #115, #117).** Root cause: every commit on those PR branches was authored under git identity `Viktor <viktor@strawberry.local>` (the subagent's worktree git config). GitHub's squash-merge UI auto-derives `Co-authored-by` from any commit whose author ≠ PR author (`duongntd99`), so it prefilled the Viktor trailer into the extended description — which was accepted at confirm-time. #116 escaped somehow (multi-commit squash apparently dropped it, or it was cleared manually). Result: live violation of global rule "Never include AI authoring references in commits."

Retroactive cleanup on main = force-push = forbidden. Fix is **forward-only: rewire subagent git identity to commit under Duong's human identity (`duongntd99`) so future squash UIs don't fabricate agent trailers.**

## Issue 1 — Agent git identity leaks into main via squash-merge Co-authored-by

**Symptom:** 3 of 4 merged work-concern commits on missmp/company-os main contain 'Co-authored-by: Viktor <viktor@strawberry.local>'. Live rule violation of global 'never include AI authoring references in commits.'

**Evidence (all MERGED, on main):**
- d7241b0e (#114) — contains Co-authored-by: Viktor
- 9c9b0f2e (#115) — contains Co-authored-by: Viktor
- fc8cb0a7 (#116) — CLEAN (multi-commit squash dropped it)
- f83d4b5e (#117) — contains Co-authored-by: Viktor

**Root cause:** Subagent worktree git config has author identity set to 'Viktor <viktor@strawberry.local>' (and presumably same pattern for Jayce, Soraka, Talon, etc.). Every commit records the agent persona as author. GitHub's squash-merge UI auto-derives Co-authored-by from any PR commit whose author ≠ PR author (duongntd99) and prefills it into the extended-description box. At confirm-time the UI-pre-filled trailer landed in main.

**Why rule 'no AI authoring references' classifies this:** Agent personas are AI authoring attribution. Viktor/Jayce/etc. are Sonnet subagents, not human co-authors.

**Fix direction (Evelynn to scope):**
Option A — Commit as Duong: rewire subagent worktree git config so commits use a Duong-owned identity (e.g. duongntd99 <107381386+duongntd99@users.noreply.github.com>). Subagent persona still recorded via inbox/learnings/commit-footer-other-than-author, but git author = Duong → squash UI sees PR-author == commit-author, no Co-authored-by prefill.
Option B — Pre-merge sanitize: add a squash-time cleanup step (GitHub Action or coordinator-side script) that strips Co-authored-by trailers matching @strawberry.local before merge. Reactive; depends on discipline.
Option C — Admin cleanup helper for UI-merge case: since Duong does manual approves + clicks merge, document a pre-merge checklist reminder ('clear the extended description box of Co-authored-by: <agent>@strawberry.local lines before confirming squash'). Weak — relies on human attention at click-time.

Recommend A (structural). Option C is a stopgap that still lets this recur.

**Retroactive cleanup:** NOT possible on main without force-push (forbidden by branch protection). The 3 dirty commits stay in history as-is. Forward-only.

**Scope:** This affects both concerns. Personal-concern PRs will have the same pattern if any agent-named git identity is configured in any subagent worktree. Worth a repo-wide sweep of 'git config user.name/email' in every active worktree + .claude/agents/ agent def inspection for identity-setting instructions.

— Sona"` is parsed as `<subcommand> <rest...>`. Supported subcommands:

### `send <agent> <message...>`

Writes an inbox file at `agents/<agent>/inbox/<timestamp>-<shortid>.md` with the following schema (mirroring the former `message_agent` MCP tool):

```
---
from: <sender>
to: <agent>
priority: info
timestamp: YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM
status: pending
---

<message>
```

Sender is derived from `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set in environment. If the caller cannot be identified, the skill refuses with `agent-ops send: sender unknown` and exits 2.

**Steps to execute:**

1. Determine sender: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set, otherwise ask the caller to state who they are. If the caller cannot confirm, exit 2 with `agent-ops send: sender unknown`.
2. Delegate to `scripts/agent-ops/send.sh` via the Bash tool (mirrors `list` / `new` patterns). The script validates the target agent, creates the inbox directory, and writes the file — no Write tool is used, so the inbox-write guard does not fire.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/agent-ops/send.sh" "<agent>" "<sender>" "<message>"
```

3. Print the full path of the created inbox file (the script prints it on stdout).

### `list [--json]`

Shells out to `scripts/list-agents.sh` (with `--format json` if `--json` is given) via Bash and prints the result.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh"
# or with --json flag:
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh" --format json
```

### `new <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]`

Shells out to `scripts/new-agent.sh` with the provided arguments via Bash:

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/new-agent.sh" <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]
```

```
/agent-ops <subcommand> [args]

Subcommands:
  send <agent> <message...>   Write an inbox message to an agent
  list [--json]               List all agents (TSV or JSON)
  new <agent-name> [--role]   Scaffold a new agent directory
```

## Platform note

This skill runs identically on macOS and Windows (Git Bash). All subcommands use POSIX-portable bash via the `Bash` tool — no macOS-specific commands. Agent launching is macOS-only and is handled by `scripts/mac/launch-agent-iterm.sh`; it is not available from this skill.

## Cross-references

- `architecture/platform-parity.md` — full platform support matrix
- `plans/proposed/2026-04-08-mcp-restructure.md` — rough plan (governs Phases 2–3)
- `plans/implemented/2026-04-09-mcp-restructure-phase-1-detailed.md` — this Phase 1 spec (once promoted)

## Inbox write guard

Direct `Write` or `Edit` to `agents/*/inbox/*.md` is blocked by `scripts/hooks/pretooluse-inbox-write-guard.sh` (registered as a PreToolUse hook). Use `/agent-ops send` to deliver inbox messages — this is the only sanctioned authorship path for non-admin identities. The single permitted `Edit` is the check-inbox status flip (`status: pending` -> `status: read`); all other edits are rejected. Archival moves live under `inbox/archive/` and are unguarded. Admin bypass identities: `duongntd` and `harukainguyen1411`.

# /agent-ops — local agent operations

## Subcommand dispatch

`send evelynn "Two harness/hook flags found today during Aphelios breakdown of approved/work/2026-04-24-self-invite-to-walletstudio-org.md. Both are system-setup items per Duong's directive. Adding to your backlog.

## Flag 1 — Harness BLOCK rule ignores Rule 4 plan-direct-to-main exemption

Aphelios pushed 0314b7cc (plan breakdown landing on main). The framework fired a security warning: 'Direct push to main branch bypasses PR review; Rule 4 allows plans direct-to-main but Git Push to Default Branch is a BLOCK rule requiring explicit user authorization for this specific push.'

Commit is valid and clean — Rule 4 explicitly says plans-go-direct-to-main. The BLOCK rule is a false positive for the plans/ subtree. Needs either (a) path-scoped exemption taught to the harness, or (b) documentation that this specific warning is expected-false-positive for plan-file commits, so future agents don't self-abort.

Priority: low. Not actively blocking — agents push through the warning. Just noise.

## Flag 2 — Plan-lifecycle guard fails on heredoc-inside-command-substitution

Aphelios's first commit attempt was rejected by scripts/hooks/pretooluse-plan-lifecycle-guard.sh (bashlex AST scanner, I assume). Pattern:

    git add plan.md && git commit -m \"\$(cat <<EOF ... EOF)\"

The scanner fail-closes on this compound. Workaround she used: two separate Bash calls:

    git add plan.md
    git commit -F - <<'MSG'
    ...
    MSG

Existing learning at agents/sona/learnings/2026-04-24-plan-lifecycle-guard-blocks-sona.md captures the category. This specific heredoc-inside-\$(...) pattern should be appended as a concrete failure mode + workaround recipe so future agents find it fast.

Priority: medium. Cosmetic friction, not blocking, but adds minutes per incident and the workaround is not obvious.

## Neither is urgent

Queue alongside the existing system backlog (Co-authored-by identity fix, dual-reviewer protocol tightening, pre-compact transcript-excerpt script support, slack MCP reconnect).

— Sona"` is parsed as `<subcommand> <rest...>`. Supported subcommands:

### `send <agent> <message...>`

Writes an inbox file at `agents/<agent>/inbox/<timestamp>-<shortid>.md` with the following schema (mirroring the former `message_agent` MCP tool):

```
---
from: <sender>
to: <agent>
priority: info
timestamp: YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM
status: pending
---

<message>
```

Sender is derived from `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set in environment. If the caller cannot be identified, the skill refuses with `agent-ops send: sender unknown` and exits 2.

**Steps to execute:**

1. Determine sender: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set, otherwise ask the caller to state who they are. If the caller cannot confirm, exit 2 with `agent-ops send: sender unknown`.
2. Delegate to `scripts/agent-ops/send.sh` via the Bash tool (mirrors `list` / `new` patterns). The script validates the target agent, creates the inbox directory, and writes the file — no Write tool is used, so the inbox-write guard does not fire.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/agent-ops/send.sh" "<agent>" "<sender>" "<message>"
```

3. Print the full path of the created inbox file (the script prints it on stdout).

### `list [--json]`

Shells out to `scripts/list-agents.sh` (with `--format json` if `--json` is given) via Bash and prints the result.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh"
# or with --json flag:
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh" --format json
```

### `new <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]`

Shells out to `scripts/new-agent.sh` with the provided arguments via Bash:

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/new-agent.sh" <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]
```

```
Subcommands:

```

## Platform note

This skill runs identically on macOS and Windows (Git Bash). All subcommands use POSIX-portable bash via the `Bash` tool — no macOS-specific commands. Agent launching is macOS-only and is handled by `scripts/mac/launch-agent-iterm.sh`; it is not available from this skill.

## Cross-references

- `architecture/platform-parity.md` — full platform support matrix
- `plans/proposed/2026-04-08-mcp-restructure.md` — rough plan (governs Phases 2–3)
- `plans/implemented/2026-04-09-mcp-restructure-phase-1-detailed.md` — this Phase 1 spec (once promoted)

## Inbox write guard

Direct `Write` or `Edit` to `agents/*/inbox/*.md` is blocked by `scripts/hooks/pretooluse-inbox-write-guard.sh` (registered as a PreToolUse hook). Use `/agent-ops send` to deliver inbox messages — this is the only sanctioned authorship path for non-admin identities. The single permitted `Edit` is the check-inbox status flip (`status: pending` -> `status: read`); all other edits are rejected. Archival moves live under `inbox/archive/` and are unguarded. Admin bypass identities: `duongntd` and `harukainguyen1411`.

## Duong — 2026-04-24T10:53:46Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

# /agent-ops — local agent operations

## Subcommand dispatch

`send evelynn "Duong wants agents/memory/duong.md extended with a briefing/status-check verbosity rule. Default = high-level only; specific detail only on request. Your lane (same as the hands-off 3-track and slack-MCP items).

## New model

When Duong asks for a briefing, a status check, or any variant of 'what's going on' / 'give me the update' / 'where are we' / 'summary':

- Default: high-level only. Duong cannot keep track of every subagent, every task ID, every commit SHA, every OQ number — that is the coordinator's job to manage internally. The briefing surface is: what's shipping, what's blocked, what needs him.
- Specific details only on request. If he asks 'what did Viktor change in T.P1.12?' or 'show me the full OQ list' — then and only then go deep.
- Signal, not log. A briefing is not a transcript. Three to seven bullets is usually the right shape. If more is genuinely needed, lead with the bullets and offer to expand on request.
- Surface decisions, hide bookkeeping. Task IDs, agent IDs, commit SHAs, file paths, reviewer-protocol minutiae belong in coordinator memory — not in the user-facing brief unless Duong asked for them or they're the actionable item.
- Always include: what he must decide / approve. If nothing is blocked on him, say so plainly ('nothing blocked on you').

Applies equally to /check-inbox summaries, morning-brief output, session-resume reports, and any ad-hoc 'status' query. Overrides any default in individual skills that might produce a fuller dump.

## Where to put it

Suggest: new section 'Briefing and status-check verbosity (mandatory for coordinators)' appended after the Parallelism preference section (lines 76-86). Same 'mandatory for coordinators' framing — it governs both Evelynn and Sona, not just me.

## Commit

chore: prefix, direct-to-main (agent-config edit, not a plan). No PR.

Priority: medium — affects how both coordinators frame every status turn from now on, so sooner is better. Not urgent-blocking any runway.

— Sona"` is parsed as `<subcommand> <rest...>`. Supported subcommands:

### `send <agent> <message...>`

Writes an inbox file at `agents/<agent>/inbox/<timestamp>-<shortid>.md` with the following schema (mirroring the former `message_agent` MCP tool):

```
---
from: <sender>
to: <agent>
priority: info
timestamp: YYYY-MM-DD HH:MM
status: pending
---

<message>
```

Sender is derived from `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set in environment. If the caller cannot be identified, the skill refuses with `agent-ops send: sender unknown` and exits 2.

**Steps to execute:**

1. Determine sender: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set, otherwise ask the caller to state who they are. If the caller cannot confirm, exit 2 with `agent-ops send: sender unknown`.
2. Delegate to `scripts/agent-ops/send.sh` via the Bash tool (mirrors `list` / `new` patterns). The script validates the target agent, creates the inbox directory, and writes the file — no Write tool is used, so the inbox-write guard does not fire.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/agent-ops/send.sh" "<agent>" "<sender>" "<message>"
```

3. Print the full path of the created inbox file (the script prints it on stdout).

### `list [--json]`

Shells out to `scripts/list-agents.sh` (with `--format json` if `--json` is given) via Bash and prints the result.

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh"
# or with --json flag:
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/list-agents.sh" --format json
```

### `new <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]`

Shells out to `scripts/new-agent.sh` with the provided arguments via Bash:

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
bash "$REPO_ROOT/scripts/new-agent.sh" <agent-name> [--role "<role>"]
```

## Refusal rules

- If `send evelynn "Duong wants agents/memory/duong.md extended with a briefing/status-check verbosity rule. Default = high-level only; specific detail only on request. Your lane (same as the hands-off 3-track and slack-MCP items).

## New model

When Duong asks for a briefing, a status check, or any variant of 'what's going on' / 'give me the update' / 'where are we' / 'summary':

- Default: high-level only. Duong cannot keep track of every subagent, every task ID, every commit SHA, every OQ number — that is the coordinator's job to manage internally. The briefing surface is: what's shipping, what's blocked, what needs him.
- Specific details only on request. If he asks 'what did Viktor change in T.P1.12?' or 'show me the full OQ list' — then and only then go deep.
- Signal, not log. A briefing is not a transcript. Three to seven bullets is usually the right shape. If more is genuinely needed, lead with the bullets and offer to expand on request.
- Surface decisions, hide bookkeeping. Task IDs, agent IDs, commit SHAs, file paths, reviewer-protocol minutiae belong in coordinator memory — not in the user-facing brief unless Duong asked for them or they're the actionable item.
- Always include: what he must decide / approve. If nothing is blocked on him, say so plainly ('nothing blocked on you').

Applies equally to /check-inbox summaries, morning-brief output, session-resume reports, and any ad-hoc 'status' query. Overrides any default in individual skills that might produce a fuller dump.

## Where to put it

Suggest: new section 'Briefing and status-check verbosity (mandatory for coordinators)' appended after the Parallelism preference section (lines 76-86). Same 'mandatory for coordinators' framing — it governs both Evelynn and Sona, not just me.

## Commit

chore: prefix, direct-to-main (agent-config edit, not a plan). No PR.

— Sona"` is empty, print the subcommand help below and exit 0.
- If the subcommand is unrecognized, refuse with `agent-ops: unknown subcommand <name>` and exit 2.
- If `send` cannot determine a sender, refuse with `agent-ops send: sender unknown` and exit 2.
- If `send` target agent directory does not exist, refuse with `agent-ops send: unknown agent <name>` and exit 2.

**Subcommand help (printed when arguments empty):**

```
/agent-ops <subcommand> [args]

Subcommands:
  send <agent> <message...>   Write an inbox message to an agent
  list [--json]               List all agents (TSV or JSON)
  new <agent-name> [--role]   Scaffold a new agent directory
```

## Platform note

This skill runs identically on macOS and Windows (Git Bash). All subcommands use POSIX-portable bash via the `Bash` tool — no macOS-specific commands. Agent launching is macOS-only and is handled by `scripts/mac/launch-agent-iterm.sh`; it is not available from this skill.

## Cross-references

- `architecture/platform-parity.md` — full platform support matrix
- `plans/proposed/2026-04-08-mcp-restructure.md` — rough plan (governs Phases 2–3)
- `plans/implemented/2026-04-09-mcp-restructure-phase-1-detailed.md` — this Phase 1 spec (once promoted)

## Inbox write guard

Direct `Write` or `Edit` to `agents/*/inbox/*.md` is blocked by `scripts/hooks/pretooluse-inbox-write-guard.sh` (registered as a PreToolUse hook). Use `/agent-ops send` to deliver inbox messages — this is the only sanctioned authorship path for non-admin identities. The single permitted `Edit` is the check-inbox status flip (`status: pending` -> `status: read`); all other edits are rejected. Archival moves live under `inbox/archive/` and are unguarded. Admin bypass identities: `duongntd` and `harukainguyen1411`.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

     ```bash
     #!/usr/bin/env bash
     set -euo pipefail
     REPO_ROOT="$(cd "$(dirname "$0")/../../.." && pwd)"
     cd "$REPO_ROOT"
     exec ./tools/decrypt.sh \
       --target "secrets/work/runtime/<name>.env" \
     ```

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T11:45:57Z

Let me verify the premise before pivoting — if an existing endpoint actually handles "super-admin invites to arbitrary org", the whole tse PR cluster (#2108, #2109, T3-T6) becomes redundant.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T11:50:27Z

I checked — Duong's premise runs into a rego policy detail:

**The "api exists" is half-true.** `POST /v3/orgs/:orgId/invites` → `InviteUsers()` handler exists in `api/v3/invites.go`. But it's mounted under the `org` echo group with `CheckPermissionForOrg()` middleware, which resolves the caller's role via:

```
has_role = role { role = input.user.org_roles[org_id] }
```

Roles are **per-org scoped**. A SuperAdmin-in-own-org hitting `POST /v3/orgs/:otherOrgId/invites` gets `has_role == ""` → deny. There is no global-SuperAdmin bypass in the rego (only `ReadAllOrgs` / `ReadAllOrgsNoPersonalData` special roles, both GET-only).

That's *why* the ADR proposed a new route under the `/v3/superadmin/*` admin group — that group uses `CheckPermissionSuperAdmin()` which does a global check (same middleware as `TransferProjectToNewOrgHandler`, etc.). The new handler is deliberately thin: 133 lines in PR #2108, and T3 just makes it call the same `a.InviteUsers()` app-layer function. We're **not** forking invite logic; we're mounting a SuperAdmin-gated alias of it.

Your options now:

1. **Keep the new endpoint as-designed** (status quo: PR #2108/#2109 proceed, T3 implements the thin wrapper calling `a.InviteUsers()`).
   cleanest; no authz risk; 133 lines of boilerplate.
2. **Broaden the rego** — introduce a `global_superadmin` role that bypasses the `org_roles[org_id]` check for all endpoints.
   balanced but touches global authz; affects every org-scoped endpoint, not just invite; needs authz review.
3. **Re-mount the existing `InviteUsers` under the superadmin group too** — register `admin.POST("/invite-user-to-org/:orgId", InviteUsers(a))` with SuperAdmin middleware instead of writing a new handler. Requires refactoring `InviteUsers` to accept orgId from path rather than from `GetOrgFromContext`.
   quickest; but it bifurcates one handler across two middleware chains and makes the app-layer contract fuzzier.

**Pick: 1.** The new endpoint is already the minimum (≈ 133-line thin wrapper) and the PRs are open, green, and waiting on your approve. Option 2 is a bigger authz surface change than Duong's intent; option 3 saves maybe 80 lines but muddies the handler's permission model.

Want to proceed with 1 (unblock by approving #2108 then #2109), or did you have specifically option 3 in mind?
