Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/end-session

# /end-session — top-level session close

You are closing a top-level Claude Code session. This skill wraps the full close-session protocol into a deterministic checklist. Follow every step in order. Do not skip steps. Do not reorder.

## Argument

`` is the agent name whose session is being closed. If empty, refuse immediately with `end-session: agent name required — pass the agent name as an argument (e.g. /end-session evelynn)` and exit. If `` is set to something other than a valid agent name (no matching `agents/<name>/` directory), refuse with `end-session: unknown agent <name>` and exit.

## Step 0 — Context probe

Run these Bash commands in a single call and keep the output in mind:

```
pwd
git status --short
git log -1 --oneline
date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ
```

If the working tree has uncommitted changes unrelated to the session close (files outside `agents/<agent>/`, `scripts/`, `CLAUDE.md`, `.gitignore`), stop and report: `end-session: working tree dirty with unrelated files — commit or stash before closing`. Do not proceed.

## Step 1 — Discover source jsonl

Run the cleaner in dry-run mode (just discovery, no write) using the Bash tool:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto --out /tmp/end-session-probe.md
```

Note: for Phase 1, the cleaner does not have a separate dry-run flag. The `/tmp/` output path is a throwaway probe. After the probe, delete `/tmp/end-session-probe.md`.

Capture the stderr for any `CLEANER: chain ambiguous` warnings and relay them to the agent for confirmation before proceeding.

## Step 2 — Clean transcript

Run the cleaner for real:

```
python scripts/clean-jsonl.py --agent <agent> --session auto
```

The cleaner writes to the default path `agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md`.

- On exit code 0: record the output path from the cleaner's stdout.
- On exit code 1: report the error and stop. Do not proceed to any further step.
- On exit code 2: report the internal error and stop.
- On exit code 3: report the secret match verbatim, STOP IMMEDIATELY, do not stage any files, do not run the commit step. Escalate to Duong via the final report.

## Step 3 — Stage the transcript

```
git add agents/<agent>/transcripts/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<short-uuid>.md
```

Verify the file is staged with `git status --short`.

## Step 4 — (reserved for condenser, no-op in Phase 1)

Log `end-session: condenser step skipped — Phase 2 will wire Syndra's component A here` and continue.

## Step 5 — Journal append

Prompt the invoking agent (you, running this skill) to append their first-person reflection for this session to `agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`. Rules:

- Append only. Do NOT overwrite existing content.
- First-person voice. Not a transcript copy.
- 10–30 lines typical. No hard cap.

Use the Write tool if the file does not exist, Edit (append) if it does. After writing, stage the file:

```
git add agents/<agent>/journal/cli-<YYYY-MM-DD>.md
```

## Step 6 — Remember handoff

**If agent == evelynn:** Skip the `remember:remember` plugin entirely (it has a single-file race surface unsafe under concurrent close — see D6 in `plans/approved/2026-04-18-evelynn-memory-sharding.md`). Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md` where `<short-uuid>` is the UUID from Step 2's transcript path. Content: a structured 5–10 line handoff — date, session number, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers. Stage:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "remember:remember bypassed for evelynn — shard written to last-sessions/<short-uuid>.md" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Invoke the `remember:remember` skill via the Skill tool. This is the primary handoff mechanism — it writes `.remember/remember.md` with a structured snapshot of what is done, what is next, and any non-obvious context. The Remember plugin's `SessionStart` hook loads this automatically at the start of the next session.

```
Skill: remember:remember
```

Stage the output file:

```
git add .remember/remember.md
```

If the `remember` plugin is not installed or the skill is unavailable, fall back to writing `agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md` manually with a 5–10 line terse handoff (date, what happened, open threads, dangling commits or PRs, blockers). Stage with `git add -f agents/<agent>/memory/last-session.md`. Note "remember step skipped — plugin not available, used last-session.md fallback" in the final report.

## Step 6b — Update open-threads.md + regenerate INDEX.md (coordinators only)

**Ordering invariant:** Step 6 (write shard) MUST complete before Step 6b because the shard is the source for both open-threads.md and INDEX.md updates. Step 6b MUST complete before Step 9 (commit + push) so all three artifacts land atomically in one commit.

**If agent is a coordinator (evelynn OR sona):** Run the following after Step 6 completes.

1. Parse the shard's `## Open threads into next session` section (or `## Open threads` section). For each thread listed:
   - If resolved/closed: remove or mark closed the matching `## <thread>` section in `agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md`.
   - If new or still-open: add or update its `## <thread>` section with the shard UUID as a pointer and a status one-liner.
   - You are the coordinator — you confirm the diff before writing. Hand-curation is the value here.
   - If `open-threads.md` does not exist yet, create it from scratch.

2. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/open-threads.md
   ```

3. Regenerate `last-sessions/INDEX.md`:
   ```
   bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only
   ```

4. Stage:
   ```
   git add agents/<agent>/memory/last-sessions/INDEX.md
   ```

If Step 6b fails partway (e.g., `--index-only` errors), the shard written in Step 6 is already staged and recoverable. Do NOT abort the session close — log the failure and proceed to Step 9 with only the shard staged. Recovery path: run `bash scripts/memory-consolidate.sh <agent> --index-only`, stage `INDEX.md`, and amend the next commit manually.

**If agent is NOT a coordinator (non-coordinator agents — Sonnet subagents, Lissandra standalone, etc.):** Step 6b is a no-op. Skip entirely and proceed to Step 7.

## Step 7 — Memory refresh

**If agent == evelynn:** Do NOT touch `agents/evelynn/memory/evelynn.md`. Instead, write a new shard at `agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md` (same UUID from Step 2) containing:
- A `## Session YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>)` heading.
- One-line summary of the session.
- Any delta notes to Key Context or Working Patterns that should be folded in at next consolidation.

Stage the shard:

```
git add agents/evelynn/memory/sessions/<short-uuid>.md
```

Note "evelynn memory shard written to sessions/<short-uuid>.md — consolidation will fold into evelynn.md at next boot" in the final report.

**If agent != evelynn:** Review `agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md`. If anything material changed this session (new working patterns, new known issues, sessions list), update it:

- Append a new session row to the `## Sessions` list with the format `- YYYY-MM-DD (SN, <mode>): <one-line summary>`.
- Prune stale entries if the file exceeds 50 lines. Remove the oldest session rows first.
- Update `## Key context` or `## Working patterns` only if the change is durable.

If nothing material changed, skip the update but still state "no memory changes this session" in the final report. Stage if modified:

```
git add agents/<agent>/memory/<agent>.md
```

## Step 8 — Learnings

If this session produced a generalizable lesson (something a future instance of this agent or a sibling agent would benefit from), write it to `agents/<agent>/learnings/<YYYY-MM-DD>-<topic>.md` and add a one-line reference to `agents/<agent>/learnings/index.md`.

If no learning, skip and state "no learnings this session" in the final report.

Stage any new learning files:

```
git add agents/<agent>/learnings/
```

## Step 9 — Commit + push

Build the commit message. Format:

```
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session
```

Use `cli` as the platform for Claude Code sessions. Use HEREDOC form:

```
git commit -m "$(cat <<'EOF'
chore: <agent> session closing — transcript, handoff, memory, learnings for YYYY-MM-DD <platform> session

Co-Authored-By: Claude Opus 4.6 (1M context) <noreply@anthropic.com>
EOF
)"
```

Then push:

```
git push
```

**If the pre-push hook rejects the commit** (wrong prefix, gitleaks hit, anything): STOP. Do not retry. Do not rewrite the commit. Report the error verbatim in the final report and exit with `end-session: commit rejected — manual intervention required`.

**If the push fails because main moved forward**: pull with merge (never rebase per CLAUDE.md git rules), then re-push. One retry only. If the second push fails, stop and report.

## Step 10 — Final report

Print a single-paragraph summary to the agent's output:

- Cleaned transcript path
- Commit hash
- Push status
- Journal / remember handoff / memory / learnings status (which were updated, which were skipped)
- Any warnings from the chain-walk or non-fatal errors along the way

Then exit. Do not close the session yourself — Duong or Evelynn explicitly ends the session after reviewing the report.

# /check-inbox — read and archive pending inbox messages

Implements plans/in-progress/2026-04-20-strawberry-inbox-channel.md §3.4.

## Purpose

Scan `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` for files with `status: pending`, display each
message, **archive** them to `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/` with
`status: read` and a `read_at` timestamp. Enforces the pending-only invariant
of the main inbox directory.

After running, `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.

## Step 0 — Identify the coordinator

Resolve agent name in this order:

1. `CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` environment variable (set by `claude --agent <name>`)
2. `STRAWBERRY_AGENT` environment variable
3. `.claude/settings.json` `.agent` field (case-insensitive)

If none of the above resolves a name, refuse:

```
check-inbox: cannot identify agent — set CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME or STRAWBERRY_AGENT
```

## Step 1 — List pending messages

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
ls "$REPO_ROOT/agents/<AGENT>/inbox/"*.md 2>/dev/null || echo "(no .md files)"
```

For each `.md` file found at the top level of `inbox/` (not in `archive/`
subdirectories), read its frontmatter and collect those with `status: pending`.

If none are pending, print:

```
No pending messages for <AGENT>.
```

...and stop (exit 0).

## Step 2 — Display each pending message

For each pending message file, print a formatted block:

```
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
From:      <from>
Priority:  <priority>
Timestamp: <timestamp>
File:      agents/<agent>/inbox/<filename>
──────────────────────────────────────────────────
<body text — everything after the closing --- frontmatter fence>
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
```

## Step 3 — Archive each message

For each pending message, perform the following steps **in order** (the
ordering is critical for watcher filter discipline — write `status: read`
before the `mv` so a concurrent watcher event sees the file already read):

### Step 3a — Rewrite frontmatter in place

Use the Edit tool:

- Change `status: pending` → `status: read`
- Add a new line `read_at: <ISO-8601 UTC timestamp>` directly after the
  `status: read` line.

Use `date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ` via Bash for the timestamp.

Do not remove any other frontmatter fields. Do not alter the body text.

Example of updated frontmatter:

```yaml
---
from: sona
to: evelynn
priority: normal
timestamp: 2026-04-21T14:02:00Z
status: read
read_at: 2026-04-21T14:05:33Z
---
```

### Step 3b — Compute the archive path

- Derive `<YYYY-MM>` from the file's `timestamp:` frontmatter field.
  - Parse the first 7 characters (e.g. `2026-04` from `2026-04-21T14:02:00Z`).
  - Fallback: if `timestamp:` is absent, use the file's mtime:
    `date -r <file> +%Y-%m 2>/dev/null || date +%Y-%m`
- Archive path: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<original-filename>`

### Step 3c — Move the file

```bash
mkdir -p "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>"
mv "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/<filename>" "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<filename>"
```

**Concurrency guard:** if the `mv` fails because the source file is already
gone (rare — would require two parallel `/check-inbox` runs on the same inbox),
skip and continue. Do not abort. This is idempotent by design.

## Step 4 — Summary

After processing all pending messages, print a one-line summary:

```
check-inbox: archived <N> message(s) for <AGENT>.
```

Post-condition: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.
The `archive/` subdirectory is the only remaining populated location.

## Refusal rules

- If the agent directory `agents/<AGENT>/` does not exist, refuse:
  `check-inbox: unknown agent <name>`
- If `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` does not exist, print:
  `check-inbox: inbox directory not found for <AGENT> — no messages`
  and exit 0 (not an error; the inbox may never have been written to).
- Never write secrets into any message body.
- Never modify any field other than `status` and adding `read_at`.
- Never write to `archive/` from the `send` path — the `send` path in
  `/agent-ops` always writes to the flat `inbox/` directory only.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T02:28:43Z

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T02:29:52Z

Three classes of hook failure on Karma's plan — nothing semantic, all structural:

**1. Section heading.** `tests_required: true` requires a `## Test plan` section. Karma wrote `## 5. Test plan`. The hook regex appears to want the exact heading without a leading number. Tiny rename.

**2. Stray `h)` time unit.** The §D4 check looks for anything-other-than-`estimate_minutes` as a time unit in §Tasks. Somewhere in Karma's task prose there's a substring matching `h)` (possibly false-positive on an English phrase like "fresh h…" or a hex code). Haven't located it yet — Syndra will grep.

**3. `cited path does not exist` cascade (the bulk of the noise).** The pre-lint scans every backtick-wrapped token in the plan body and tries to `test -f` it relative to repo root. It flags:
- **Prospective paths** — files this plan proposes to create (`scripts/hooks/pretooluse-work-scope-identity.sh`, `scripts/post-reviewer-comment.sh`, `scripts/hooks/agent-identity-default.sh`). Karma added `<!-- orianna: ok -->` on the `files:` lines but missed prose mentions.
- **Non-paths mistaken for paths** — backtick tokens that aren't files at all: `user.name`, `user.email`, `GIT_AUTHOR_*`, `GIT_COMMITTER_*`, `PreToolUse.Bash`, `[:/]missmp/` (regex fragment), `missmp/company-os` (external repo slug), `anonymity_scan_text` (function name), bare filenames like `pre-commit-reviewer-anonymity.sh` (exists, but the script wants full relative path `scripts/hooks/pre-commit-reviewer-anonymity.sh`).

Plus one real bug: `awk i/o error on scripts/hooks/tests/` — the validator tried `test -f` on a directory and crashed mid-scan.

The fix convention per the hook's own hint (`add <!-- orianna: ok --> to suppress for prospective paths`) is suppression markers on every affected line. Mechanical but wide.

Syndra is applying fixes now in background, committing once clean. This is a pre-existing design tension — the prelint is aggressive and doesn't distinguish "word-in-backticks" from "path-in-backticks." Worth noting as a follow-up thread (same class as the AST scanner heredoc false-positive already in open-threads).

## Duong — 2026-04-24T02:31:05Z

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T02:32:34Z

Honest answer: **I did not invoke Orianna yet.** The commit that hit the wall was my own `chore:` commit to save the OQ1 edit to the plan file before dispatching Orianna. That commit hit a *separate* pre-commit hook — `pre-commit-plan-structure.sh` (via `lib-plan-structure.sh`) — which fires on every plan-file edit regardless of whether a promotion is happening.

On whether this should still exist: it's a genuine design-tension you're pointing at. The layout today is:

- **Orianna** = semantic + structural gate at **promotion transitions** (`proposed → approved → …`). Sole agent-checklist gate.
- **`pre-commit-plan-structure.sh`** = mechanical structural checks at **every plan edit commit**, wired in per the 2026-04-20 "shift-left structural checks prevent gate pileup" learning. The rationale was: catch structural drift early so Orianna's gate doesn't accumulate noise.

The learning argued for shift-left. Your current instinct argues the other way: trust Orianna as the one true gate, kill the mechanical pre-lint. Both are reasonable. The practical problem right now is the pre-lint's path-detection is overmatched — it treats *any backtick-wrapped token* as a candidate file path, so `user.name`, `[:/]missmp/`, `GIT_AUTHOR_*`, etc. all trip it. Same false-positive class as the heredoc AST scanner issue already in open-threads.

Three paths forward:

1. **Retire the pre-commit plan-structure hook entirely.** Orianna becomes the sole gate. Plans can be in any shape during authoring; structural cleanup happens at promotion. Simplest; loses shift-left benefit. Needs an ADR.
2. **Narrow the path-detection.** Only flag tokens that look path-shaped (contain `/` or end in `.sh`/`.md`/`.py` etc.), ignore config keys and env vars. Keeps shift-left, drops false positives. Small scope.
3. **Status quo + suppression markers.** What Syndra is doing right now. Works but feels like busywork.

Stop Syndra and route this to an ADR instead? Or let Syndra finish this one plan under status quo and queue option 1 or 2 as a separate follow-up ADR?

## Duong — 2026-04-24T02:47:21Z

we did have a fix for the git race right? with the worktree?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T02:48:05Z

Yes — `isolation: "worktree"` on the Agent tool call. Spawns a temp git worktree on a separate branch, agent commits there, parent merges on return. Structural fix for the parallel-subagent commit-race problem we materialized on 2026-04-23 (learning: `2026-04-23-parallel-subagent-write-race-materialized.md`).

It's auto-applied for `aphelios`, `kayn`, `xayah`, `caitlyn` via `scripts/hooks/agent-default-isolation.sh` reading `default_isolation: worktree` frontmatter. Ekko and Syndra are NOT in the opt-in list, and I did NOT pass `isolation: "worktree"` explicitly on either dispatch. My "disjoint tree" rationale was weaker than actual isolation — the file scopes don't collide, but `git commit` on a shared working tree still contends for the index lock and can race.

Realistic risk: low but nonzero. Ekko's a fast 4-file archival; Syndra is sweeping edits across many files (slower). If their commit windows overlap we could get an index lock fail or (worse) one of them staging the other's unintended files.

Options:
1. **Stop Syndra** (the slower one), re-dispatch with `isolation: "worktree"`. Wastes a few minutes of her work but eliminates race risk.
2. **Let both finish**, reconcile if a race surfaces. Small chance of a retry cost.
3. **Stop both, re-dispatch both with isolation.** Cleanest but most waste.

Auto mode preference is execute-on-reasonable-assumptions. Risk is low given Ekko's short runtime. I'd let them finish and reconcile if needed — but say the word if you want me to stop one or both.

## Duong — 2026-04-24T02:50:28Z

i meant why did you not have the worktree for all agents but only the selected on like Kayn etc

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T02:51:02Z

Good question, and the honest answer is: it's opt-in because the plan that introduced it (`plans/proposed/personal/2026-04-23-subagent-worktree-and-edit-only.md` — still awaiting your review) was scoped to **breakdown-agent inline-edit discipline** (aphelios/kayn/xayah/caitlyn: force them to edit parent plans inline rather than create sibling `-tasks.md` / `-breakdown.md` files). Race-prevention was a happy side-effect, not the design goal.

There's no principled reason to limit worktree isolation to those four for race-prevention purposes. It's a universal benefit: any two Sonnet subagents committing on the same tree can race, regardless of whether they're writing plans or code.

**The one real constraint** is the nested-worktree issue per learning `2026-04-11-nested-worktree-permissions.md`: if a subagent spawned *into* a worktree then dispatches its own subagent with `isolation: worktree`, permissions break (triple-nested). But for coordinator-dispatched executors (the dominant case — Evelynn → Sonnet executor) it's clean: single level of nesting, no permission issues.

Tradeoffs of flipping the default to universal:
- **Pro:** structural race prevention across the board, no more concurrent-commit-entanglement like the one that just bit us (learnings 2026-04-23-parallel-subagent-write-race-materialized + 2026-04-23-concurrent-agent-commit-entanglement).
- **Pro:** dirty working tree in one agent's worktree doesn't contaminate another's (which is exactly what happened today — orphan work from Lucian/Senna sessions was sitting in the shared tree when Ekko + Syndra spawned).
- **Con:** every subagent spawn costs a worktree create + merge-back. Small cost, but it's per-spawn.
- **Con:** some tasks legitimately need shared-tree access (e.g., full-repo probes). Those would need to explicitly opt OUT via `isolation: none` or similar.
- **Con:** Skarner/Yuumi-class read-only minions don't need isolation overhead.

My read: **universal default for coordinator-dispatched executors, with an explicit opt-out for read-only or multi-repo probe agents.** That's a real ADR — not a one-liner. Worth commissioning Swain or Karma to write it.

Want me to promote this thread to an ADR now, or batch it after the current chain (Ekko cleanup + Orianna promotion) lands?

yes. have the worktree isolation on agents who needs it. Yuumi is not read class though if I remember correctly

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:05:58Z

**ADR brief — `plans/proposed/personal/2026-04-24-universal-worktree-isolation.md`**

**Problem** — 3 race incidents in a week, all same root: coordinator-dispatched subagents share one working tree. 2026-04-23 parallel write race (Ekko #33 vs #32 commit-SHAs diverged), 2026-04-23 commit entanglement (pre-commit hook re-staging sibling files across invocations), 2026-04-24 today (Ekko crash would have bundled Lucian's orphan work + PR104 screenshots + unrelated `karma.md` edits into his cleanup commit). Current opt-in set (aphelios/kayn/xayah/caitlyn) was framed around breakdown-agent inline-edit discipline, not race-prevention — wrong problem class.

**Decision** — Flip `scripts/hooks/agent-default-isolation.sh` from opt-in to opt-out. Subagents auto-isolated unless: (a) caller passes `isolation:` explicitly (caller wins), (b) agent-def frontmatter has `default_isolation: none`, (c) agent is in opt-out allowlist, or (d) parent is already in a worktree (nested-dispatch guard from 2026-04-11 learning — detects via `git rev-parse --git-dir != --git-common-dir`).

**Opt-out allowlist** — Only **Skarner** (read-only search mode) and **Orianna** (script-only, never reached by Agent tool). Explicitly kept in the default-isolated set: Yuumi (she writes), Ekko (today's incident), Lissandra (writes near coordinator close = race-prone), Akali (writes QA artifacts), all planners, all implementers, all reviewers. Azir flagged that "Explore" isn't in the `.claude/agents/` roster — it's a tool-class, not an agent — so no action needed there.

**Merge-back protocol** — 3 cases, coordinator-owned: (a) no commits → harness auto-cleans, (b) commits → `git merge --ff-only`, fallback to `--no-ff` per Rule 11, (c) parallel conflict → fail loud on plan files, prefer shards on memory, re-dispatch on code. Proposes a helper `scripts/subagent-merge-back.sh` to encapsulate the three cases.

**Migration** — Leave existing `default_isolation: worktree` frontmatter on the 4 breakdown agents (redundant but harmless documentation-of-intent). Preserve `Write`-removed-from-tools on those 4 (D1A inline-edit subgoal — orthogonal to isolation). Proposed ordering in a single PR: (i) merge-back helper + coordinator docs, (ii) xfail tests, (iii) hook flip. Rule 12 requires xfail commit on same branch as impl, so one-PR is the honest shape.

**Tests** — 8 xfail invariants: INV-1 default applies broadly, INV-2 Skarner untouched, INV-3 caller override always wins, INV-4 nested-dispatch guard, INV-5 frontmatter opt-out honored, INV-6 parallel non-race, INV-7/8 behavioral spawn checks for Skarner and Yuumi specifically (the brief's call-out).

**Three OQs needing your call:**

1. **Skarner-write mode.** Proposed: fully opt out, callers pass `isolation: "worktree"` explicitly when calling her in write mode (coordinator discipline). Alternatives: keep in default-isolated set (wasteful worktree per search), or split into `skarner-search` / `skarner-write` agent defs. Azir recommends the coordinator-discipline approach.

2. **Merge-back mechanism.** Proposed: explicit `scripts/subagent-merge-back.sh` helper that coordinators invoke after each returned subagent. Alternative: a PostToolUse Agent auto-merge hook (zero coordinator overhead but harder to reason about mid-merge failures). Azir recommends start-with-explicit, iterate to auto if the manual burden proves real.

3. **Migration ordering.** Proposed: single PR with the ordering above. Alternative: split across PRs. Azir recommends single PR (xfail-on-same-branch plus docs-before-hook-flip both argue for atomic).

Which way on each?

## Duong — 2026-04-24T03:06:01Z

btw, do you not read the ADR yourself and just relay the questions to me?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:06:45Z

Fair callout. I did read it, but I defaulted to relaying Azir's questions verbatim instead of actually taking a position. That's coordinator-as-messenger — the exact anti-pattern. Taking positions now:

**OQ1 (Skarner modes) — I disagree with Azir's recommendation.** He proposes caller-discipline (coordinators remember to pass `isolation: "worktree"` for Skarner-write). But the entire argument for flipping opt-in to opt-out was that caller-discipline loses at scale — today's Ekko incident is the proof. Reaching back for discipline on Skarner-write breaks the same principle. **My call: Option (b) — keep Skarner in the default-isolated set.** Isolating a read-only search is ~50ms waste per dispatch; the harness auto-cleans the worktree when no commits land. That cost is trivial against the cost of maintaining a two-mode behavioral contract that one day bites us the same way. Uniform behavior > shaving 50ms on read-only paths.

**OQ2 (merge-back mechanism) — I agree with Azir, different reasoning.** He says "start explicit, iterate later." My version: start explicit because **we need observability on a brand-new mechanism across the whole roster**. An auto-merge PostToolUse hook hides failure modes in places we haven't discovered yet. Ship `scripts/subagent-merge-back.sh` as a coordinator-invoked helper; if after a week coordinators are calling it identically every single time with no branching, THEN collapse to auto. Classic iterate-when-the-work-clears.

**OQ3 (migration ordering) — I agree with Azir.** Single PR. Rule 12 forces xfail-commit and impl-commit on the same branch, which tips the honest scales toward one PR anyway. Splitting would stack PRs (merge-back helper → xfails → hook flip) and add ceremony without meaningful review isolation. One PR, three commits, clear sequence.

**Summary call for the ADR:** OQ1 overridden to Option (b); OQ2 and OQ3 accept Azir's recommendations. Want me to write these decisions into the ADR body as resolved-OQ notes before Orianna promotes it, or hold the promotion until you weigh in on whether to override my override?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:10:16Z

Skarner-write is **vestigial**. Here's what I found:

**Her own agent def** documents two modes — search + write — with tools `Read, Glob, Grep, Bash, Write, Edit`. Write-mode protocol is: caller provides agent-name/date/summary, Skarner writes to `agents/<name>/memory/<YYYY-MM-DD>.md`.

**But every other document treats her as read-only:**
- `agent-network.md` line 65: "Memory excavator — **read-only** searches"
- `agent-network.md` line 131: "Every agent except Skarner and Yuumi **must** write to two places at session end" — she's EXEMPT from end-session writes
- Evelynn + Sona CLAUDE.md delegation trees: only "memory retrieval" listed, no write
- Swain's agent def: "use Skarner when you need to recall past memories" (search only)
- Every grep hit for actual usage is `delegate topic searches to Skarner` — zero write-mode invocations anywhere

The modern write paths cover what Skarner-write was supposed to do:
- `/end-subagent-session` — Sonnet subagent session close
- `/end-session` — coordinator session close
- Lissandra — coordinator pre-compact consolidation
- `scripts/memory-consolidate.sh` — shard consolidation

So Skarner-write is dead code in her definition. No caller invokes it; the actual work is routed through dedicated skills/agents.

**Proposal:** retire Skarner-write. Strip Write/Edit from her tools, remove the "Mode: Write" section from her def, and OQ1 collapses entirely — she's cleanly opt-out as a pure read-only memory excavator. This also resolves the slight dissonance between her def and agent-network.md treating her differently.

Greenlight me to retire Skarner-write as part of the ADR resolution? That way the ADR's opt-out list has no "but-what-about-write-mode" asterisk, and the two docs agree.

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:17:34Z

Lissandra working. Will verify sentinel + commit when she reports.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:43:44Z

**Senna → REQUEST CHANGES on PR #35.** One critical bug, three important issues — all fair. Summary:

- **C1 (critical, blocking)** — T1 regex in `pretooluse-work-scope-identity.sh:43` misses `git -c user.name=X commit` and `git -C <path> commit`. Plan explicitly named these as attack vectors, so this is a spec violation not a nit. Pattern only matches dash-prefixed tokens between `git` and `commit`; `-c KEY=VAL` and `-C <path>` carry non-dash positional args, fall through, hook exits 0 silently.
- **I2** — T3 denylist drift: plan required single-source-of-truth from `_ANONYMITY_AGENT_NAMES` lib; impl duplicated 17 names inline. Lucian flagged this too in her review — two independent catches on the same gap.
- **I1** — "fail-closed" claim in the plan is overstated. Hook exits 0 silently on missing python3, JSON parse failure, absent origin. Only the config-write path actually blocks. Pick one: tighten hook or amend plan wording.
- **I3** — Test coverage is happy-path biased: no test for `-c` / `-C` bypass, no body-probe, no denylist sweep, INV-4a pattern-matches docstrings.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:50:39Z

Test message posted to `C0ANVLZQ17X` ✓.

**MCP structure finding:** the Slack MCP at `mcps/slack/scripts/start.sh` is a **one-line shim around the upstream `@modelcontextprotocol/server-slack` npm package** — it doesn't define its own tools. The whole server is `exec env SLACK_BOT_TOKEN="$TOKEN" npx -y @modelcontextprotocol/server-slack`. That means adding a real MCP tool called `message_duong` requires either forking the upstream package or writing a new custom MCP server from scratch — medium-effort engineering for essentially a channel-ID lookup shortcut.

Applying the simplicity-first principle I just baked in: three paths, ranked simplest-first:

**Path A — Memory entry (simplest, recommended).** Add `C0ANVLZQ17X → Duong's DM` to my coordinator memory (`agents/memory/duong.md` or a dedicated `agents/memory/slack-channels.md`). Future messages call the existing `mcp__slack__slack_post_message` with the channel ID baked in at call-site. No new code, no tooling, just a one-line memory entry. Every Evelynn/Sona session that reads memory on startup will know the channel. **Complexity: zero new moving parts.**

**Path B — Slash-command skill.** Add `.claude/skills/message-duong/SKILL.md` wrapping `slack_post_message`. I invoke as `/message-duong <text>`. Slightly nicer ergonomics, still uses the existing MCP tool underneath. **Complexity: one skill file + one-line invocation pattern.**

**Path C — Custom MCP server.** Fork or write a new Slack MCP that declares `message_duong` as a first-class tool. **Complexity: ~50-150 LOC Node/TS, maintenance burden, duplicates upstream.** Not justified unless you have other reasons to own a custom server.

My recommendation is **A**. You get the "don't list channels" outcome without writing any code. If after a week of usage you feel an explicit `/message-duong` skill would be cleaner, we layer B on top — still not touching C.

Do you want A now (I can add the memory entry in ~30 seconds and dogfood it immediately), or A+B, or are you set on the real MCP tool (C)?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:51:58Z

That's a real finding I should have caught from the response payload — the `"user":"U03KDE6SS9J"` field in the post response IS your user ID, and Slack routes notifications by underlying author, not by the `bot_profile` label. That means the memory entry I was about to commit is **wrong** — it says "post to `C0ANVLZQ17X` to reach Duong" but that won't actually reach you. Reverting the edit before it compounds:

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:52:17Z

Reverted — nothing committed. Now the real problem:

**Root cause.** The `xoxp-` token is YOUR user token. Even though the `bot_profile` response decoration shows "Sona — Duong's secretary," Slack's notification routing looks at the underlying author (`user: U03KDE6SS9J` = you), not the decoration. Net effect: no channel will ever ping you when messages come through this token.

**What actually solves "agent pings me":**

1. **Use a proper bot token (`xoxb-`).** Requires creating a real Slack app in your workspace with bot scopes (`chat:write`, `chat:write.public`), installing it to `merisier.slack.com`, adding the bot user to channel `C0ANVLZQ17X`. Then the message genuinely comes from a bot user, not from you, and you get normal DM/mention pings. Clean long-term answer for Slack. ~10-15 min of Slack-admin UI work on your side (I can't create Slack apps), zero more code.

2. **Use the already-wired Telegram path.** The `evelynn` MCP has `TELEGRAM_CHAT_ID: "7922315245"` baked in and `mcp__evelynn__telegram_send_message` is available in this session. That almost certainly already pings you (it's a bot-to-human chat by construction). **This is the simplest test — I can fire it right now to verify.**

3. **Use Discord.** There's a Discord MCP wired too with `mcp__discord__discord_send`. Same bot-to-human dynamic as Telegram.

My recommendation — before you do the Slack-app setup, let me verify option 2 pings you. One test shot via Telegram, and if it works, Telegram becomes "agent → Duong" for the next few days while you decide whether Slack is worth the app-creation cost. Want me to try the Telegram route?

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T03:55:57Z

Yes, straightforward — and the simplest wiring is to run **two MCP instances side-by-side** rather than forking the upstream package. Here's the shape:

**The upstream constraint.** `@modelcontextprotocol/server-slack` (the npm package we wrap) takes exactly one token per process via `SLACK_BOT_TOKEN`. Forking to support both would be real engineering. But nothing stops us from running the same package **twice** with different tokens and different MCP server names.

**Proposed layout.**

1. Current misnamed file `secrets/slack-bot-token.txt` is actually `xoxp-` (user token). Rename to `secrets/slack-user-token.txt` to stop lying to ourselves.
2. You create a proper Slack app, install it to `merisier.slack.com`, grab the `xoxb-` token, drop it at `secrets/slack-bot-token.txt`.
3. Update `mcps/slack/scripts/start.sh` to take a `--token-file` arg (or split into `start-user.sh` / `start-bot.sh` — both fine).
4. `.mcp.json` gets two entries:
   ```jsonc
   "slack-bot":  { ..."start.sh --token-file .../slack-bot-token.txt",  "env": {"SLACK_TEAM_ID": "T18MLBHC5"} },
   "slack-user": { ..."start.sh --token-file .../slack-user-token.txt", "env": {"SLACK_TEAM_ID": "T18MLBHC5"} }
   ```
5. Tools appear as `mcp__slack-bot__slack_post_message` and `mcp__slack-user__slack_post_message`. I pick per call-site.

**When I'd pick which (memorize to `agents/memory/duong.md`):**

| Intent | Token | Why |
|---|---|---|
| Agent → you notification, alert, "heads up" | **bot** | Actually pings you |
| Ghost-write as you in a channel (you asked agent to draft on your behalf) | **user** | Posts under your identity |
| Read channel history for context lookup | **user** (likely broader read scope) | Bot tokens need per-channel invite |
| Post in a channel you haven't invited the bot to | **user** | Bot would 403 |
| Post as a distinct entity so colleagues don't think it's you | **bot** | Attribution matters |

**Default for "message Duong":** bot token, to `C0ANVLZQ17X`. That's the line I want memorized.

**Your part that unblocks this.** Create the Slack app + get `xoxb-` token. Slack admin UI, can't be automated from here. ~10 minutes:

1. api.slack.com/apps → Create New App → From scratch → Name "Strawberry Agents" (or anything) → pick `merisier` workspace.
2. OAuth & Permissions → Scopes → Bot Token Scopes: add `chat:write`, `chat:write.public`, `channels:history`, `channels:read`, `users:read`, `reactions:write` (matches the toolset you already have loaded).
3. Install to Workspace → approve → copy the `xoxb-...` Bot User OAuth Token.
4. Paste it to me or drop it at `secrets/slack-bot-token.txt` yourself (gitignored).
5. Invite `@Strawberry Agents` to channel `C0ANVLZQ17X` (`/invite @Strawberry Agents`).

When you have the token, I'll fire Ekko to rename the existing file, rewrite `start.sh` to accept a token-file arg, add the second `.mcp.json` entry, and commit. Session restart after that → both servers connect → I've got both tools.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T04:08:17Z

You're right. Tools encode intent at the interface layer — memory becomes a crutch we don't need. "Call `notify_duong(text)`" is unambiguous; "use `slack-bot` with `channel_id=U03KDE6SS9J`" requires me to remember the mapping every session.

Design shape question:

1. **How do we build the purposed-tools MCP?**

   a: **Single custom MCP replacing both upstream wrappers.** Thin Python or TypeScript server using `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk`. Exposes ~8–10 purposed tools (`notify_duong`, `post_as_duong`, `post_as_bot`, `read_dm_history`, `get_channel_history`, `list_users`, `list_channels`, `add_reaction`, etc.). Holds both tokens internally, routes per tool. ~120–180 LOC. One MCP server entry in `.mcp.json`. Cleanest architecture, fewest moving parts, tool names read like English verbs. Maintenance: we own the wrapper but it's tiny and Slack's Web API is stable.

   b: **Keep two upstream wrappers (bot + user) + add one small custom MCP for purposed tools only.** Three servers total. Upstream handles generic `slack_post_message` / history / reactions with the right token each; custom layer adds `notify_duong` and any other intent-specific shortcuts on top. Redundant surface — same action reachable two ways.

   c: **Skip the custom server; keep memory + two upstream wrappers (current Ekko path).** Quickest, what's in flight right now. Debt is: every agent session has to learn the mapping, and agents getting it wrong is how we just spent the last 30 minutes.

   **Pick: a.** Per simplicity-first, one server with named tools strictly beats two servers plus a memory crutch. The upstream npm package mostly wraps Slack's Web API anyway; re-implementing the ~8 endpoints we actually use is ~1 day of work and eliminates a class of runtime-decision bugs. Every future "what channel / what token" question disappears at the tool layer.

**If (a):** I redirect Ekko to stop the dual-wrapper approach and spec the custom MCP instead. Want me to also have Azir write a small ADR for it first, or just let Ekko build from a spec I hand him?

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T04:29:58Z

When Lissandra returns with the sentinel + commit, I'll verify and you can safely run `/compact`.

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T06:58:18Z

Found it. Yesterday Lux researched it and the short answer was: **no clean first-party way for an agent to self-compact its own TTY session exists today.**

Her findings (in transcript `agents/evelynn/transcripts/2026-04-23-c4af884e.md`):

- Upstream feature request open: [anthropics/claude-code#28559](https://github.com/anthropics/claude-code/issues/28559). Not implemented.
- The only sanctioned mechanism is the **built-in auto-compact** (already enabled in our `/config`). It fires at ~83.5% context window. Threshold is tunable via `CLAUDE_AUTOCOMPACT_PCT_OVERRIDE` env var (e.g. `export CLAUDE_AUTOCOMPACT_PCT_OVERRIDE=75` to fire earlier).
- A tmux-injection workaround exists but is fragile: requires tmux, races with human typing, no callback signal. Lux declined to pursue.

**No ADR or plan was written** — Lux's research closed as a one-off investigation with the recommendation "trust auto-compact, optionally lower the threshold."

So to answer directly: no proposal document exists. There's a research finding that said *the platform doesn't let us do this cleanly; use auto-compact*. If you want to formalize that into a small ADR (codifying the env-var choice + the `/pre-compact-save` skill hook chain as the canonical self-compact workflow), I can commission Lux to write one. Three paths:

1. a: Commission Lux to write a short ADR — "self-compact workflow: auto-compact + pre-compact-save" — so the decision and the env-var setting live in the repo rather than only in a transcript. Adds a concrete knob (which threshold? we've been running default 83.5%).
   b: Skip the ADR; just set `CLAUDE_AUTOCOMPACT_PCT_OVERRIDE=75` in your shell profile + note it in `agents/memory/duong.md`. Five minutes of work.
   c: Wait on upstream #28559; revisit when Anthropic ships it.

   Pick: **b**. The decision space is tiny (one env var), the research already exists, and an ADR here would be ceremony for a one-line config. If we later want agent-initiated compaction (distinct from time-based auto-compact), we revisit with a proper plan then.

Want me to apply (b)? If yes, I need one input: what threshold — 70%, 75%, 80%? (Lower = more frequent compaction = more context churn but lower risk of running out mid-task. Default 83.5% has been giving us the "pre-compact panic" window you've noticed.)

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T07:00:42Z

Before designing custom infrastructure — the harness exposes a `RemoteTrigger` tool in the deferred list. That name smells exactly like what you're describing. Loading its schema first so I'm not reinventing a wheel that already ships:

## Evelynn — 2026-04-24T07:01:37Z

`RemoteTrigger` is unrelated — it's a claude.ai API for starting *remote* Claude Code sessions from elsewhere (think cron-style remote invocation). It doesn't inject into the current TTY. Our problem stays in tmux / PTY territory.

Design space for a keystroke-fabricator:

1. **a: node-pty supervisor + Unix socket (cleanest).** New `scripts/claude-wrap.sh` wraps the `claude` binary inside a `node-pty` supervisor that owns the child's stdin/stdout. Supervisor listens on `~/.claude/inject-<pid>.sock`. Agents call `echo '/compact' | nc -U <sock>` and the keystrokes land in the child's stdin as if you'd typed them. Works for ANY slash command. No tmux dependency, no AppleScript, no TIOCSTI kernel restriction. ~200 LOC. Duong changes alias to call the wrapper instead of raw `claude`.

2. **b: tmux + send-keys (balanced).** Wrap aliases to `tmux new-session -As strawberry-evelynn -- claude`. Agents call `tmux send-keys -t strawberry-evelynn '/compact' Enter`. ~30 LOC. Lux's race objection is real but solvable: gate sends on `tmux display -p "#{pane_in_mode}"` + last-activity timestamp; only inject when pane has been idle ≥ N seconds. Works for any slash command. Requires tmux (you already have it on macOS).

3. **c: AppleScript `osascript` keystroke simulator (quick-but-debt).** `osascript -e 'tell app "System Events" to keystroke "/compact" & return'`. 5 LOC. Needs accessibility permission, macOS-only, targets the frontmost window (breaks if terminal isn't focused), and sends the keystrokes into whatever app is focused — real risk of injecting `/compact` into Cursor or Slack by mistake. Not viable.

Pick: **b** now, **a** as the upgrade if (b) races in practice. Reasoning: (b) is simple-yet-clean, ships today in ~30 LOC of wrapper + a `send_slash_command` helper, generalizes to any slash command immediately, and the "race with Duong typing" mitigates cleanly with an idle-check gate. If we outgrow (b) — e.g. want programmatic bidirectional I/O or multi-coordinator orchestration — (a) is the upgrade path without throwing (b) away.

Want me to commission a short ADR (Azir → Kayn → Jayce) for path (b)? The ADR would nail down: which alias changes, the `send_slash_command.sh` contract, the idle-gate policy (what counts as "safe to inject"), and the first user-facing slash command set to expose (just `/compact`, or also `/pre-compact-save`, `/end-session`, `/check-inbox`).

## Duong — 2026-04-24T07:17:42Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

4. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

# /check-inbox — read and archive pending inbox messages

Implements plans/in-progress/2026-04-20-strawberry-inbox-channel.md §3.4.

## Purpose

Scan `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` for files with `status: pending`, display each
message, **archive** them to `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/` with
`status: read` and a `read_at` timestamp. Enforces the pending-only invariant
of the main inbox directory.

After running, `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.

## Step 0 — Identify the coordinator

Resolve agent name in this order:

1. `CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` environment variable (set by `claude --agent <name>`)
2. `STRAWBERRY_AGENT` environment variable
3. `.claude/settings.json` `.agent` field (case-insensitive)

If none of the above resolves a name, refuse:

```
check-inbox: cannot identify agent — set CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME or STRAWBERRY_AGENT
```

## Step 1 — List pending messages

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
ls "$REPO_ROOT/agents/<AGENT>/inbox/"*.md 2>/dev/null || echo "(no .md files)"
```

For each `.md` file found at the top level of `inbox/` (not in `archive/`
subdirectories), read its frontmatter and collect those with `status: pending`.

If none are pending, print:

```
No pending messages for <AGENT>.
```

...and stop (exit 0).

## Step 2 — Display each pending message

For each pending message file, print a formatted block:

```
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
From:      <from>
Priority:  <priority>
Timestamp: <timestamp>
File:      agents/<agent>/inbox/<filename>
──────────────────────────────────────────────────
<body text — everything after the closing --- frontmatter fence>
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
```

## Step 3 — Archive each message

For each pending message, perform the following steps **in order** (the
ordering is critical for watcher filter discipline — write `status: read`
before the `mv` so a concurrent watcher event sees the file already read):

### Step 3a — Rewrite frontmatter in place

Use the Edit tool:

- Change `status: pending` → `status: read`
- Add a new line `read_at: <ISO-8601 UTC timestamp>` directly after the
  `status: read` line.

Use `date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ` via Bash for the timestamp.

Do not remove any other frontmatter fields. Do not alter the body text.

Example of updated frontmatter:

```yaml
---
from: sona
to: evelynn
priority: normal
timestamp: 2026-04-21T14:02:00Z
status: read
read_at: 2026-04-21T14:05:33Z
---
```

### Step 3b — Compute the archive path

- Derive `<YYYY-MM>` from the file's `timestamp:` frontmatter field.
  - Parse the first 7 characters (e.g. `2026-04` from `2026-04-21T14:02:00Z`).
  - Fallback: if `timestamp:` is absent, use the file's mtime:
    `date -r <file> +%Y-%m 2>/dev/null || date +%Y-%m`
- Archive path: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<original-filename>`

### Step 3c — Move the file

```bash
mkdir -p "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>"
mv "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/<filename>" "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<filename>"
```

**Concurrency guard:** if the `mv` fails because the source file is already
gone (rare — would require two parallel `/check-inbox` runs on the same inbox),
skip and continue. Do not abort. This is idempotent by design.

## Step 4 — Summary

After processing all pending messages, print a one-line summary:

```
check-inbox: archived <N> message(s) for <AGENT>.
```

Post-condition: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.
The `archive/` subdirectory is the only remaining populated location.

## Refusal rules

- If the agent directory `agents/<AGENT>/` does not exist, refuse:
  `check-inbox: unknown agent <name>`
- If `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` does not exist, print:
  `check-inbox: inbox directory not found for <AGENT> — no messages`
  and exit 0 (not an error; the inbox may never have been written to).
- Never write secrets into any message body.
- Never modify any field other than `status` and adding `read_at`.
- Never write to `archive/` from the `send` path — the `send` path in
  `/agent-ops` always writes to the flat `inbox/` directory only.

## Duong — 2026-04-24T07:58:45Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.

# /check-inbox — read and archive pending inbox messages

Implements plans/in-progress/2026-04-20-strawberry-inbox-channel.md §3.4.

## Purpose

Scan `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` for files with `status: pending`, display each
message, **archive** them to `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/` with
`status: read` and a `read_at` timestamp. Enforces the pending-only invariant
of the main inbox directory.

After running, `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.

## Step 0 — Identify the coordinator

Resolve agent name in this order:

1. `CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` environment variable (set by `claude --agent <name>`)
2. `STRAWBERRY_AGENT` environment variable
3. `.claude/settings.json` `.agent` field (case-insensitive)

If none of the above resolves a name, refuse:

```
check-inbox: cannot identify agent — set CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME or STRAWBERRY_AGENT
```

## Step 1 — List pending messages

```bash
REPO_ROOT="$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)"
ls "$REPO_ROOT/agents/<AGENT>/inbox/"*.md 2>/dev/null || echo "(no .md files)"
```

For each `.md` file found at the top level of `inbox/` (not in `archive/`
subdirectories), read its frontmatter and collect those with `status: pending`.

If none are pending, print:

```
No pending messages for <AGENT>.
```

...and stop (exit 0).

## Step 2 — Display each pending message

For each pending message file, print a formatted block:

```
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
From:      <from>
Priority:  <priority>
Timestamp: <timestamp>
File:      agents/<agent>/inbox/<filename>
──────────────────────────────────────────────────
<body text — everything after the closing --- frontmatter fence>
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━
```

## Step 3 — Archive each message

For each pending message, perform the following steps **in order** (the
ordering is critical for watcher filter discipline — write `status: read`
before the `mv` so a concurrent watcher event sees the file already read):

### Step 3a — Rewrite frontmatter in place

Use the Edit tool:

- Change `status: pending` → `status: read`
- Add a new line `read_at: <ISO-8601 UTC timestamp>` directly after the
  `status: read` line.

Use `date -u +%Y-%m-%dT%H:%M:%SZ` via Bash for the timestamp.

Do not remove any other frontmatter fields. Do not alter the body text.

Example of updated frontmatter:

```yaml
---
from: sona
to: evelynn
priority: normal
timestamp: 2026-04-21T14:02:00Z
status: read
read_at: 2026-04-21T14:05:33Z
---
```

### Step 3b — Compute the archive path

- Derive `<YYYY-MM>` from the file's `timestamp:` frontmatter field.
  - Parse the first 7 characters (e.g. `2026-04` from `2026-04-21T14:02:00Z`).
  - Fallback: if `timestamp:` is absent, use the file's mtime:
    `date -r <file> +%Y-%m 2>/dev/null || date +%Y-%m`
- Archive path: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<original-filename>`

### Step 3c — Move the file

```bash
mkdir -p "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>"
mv "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/<filename>" "agents/<AGENT>/inbox/archive/<YYYY-MM>/<filename>"
```

**Concurrency guard:** if the `mv` fails because the source file is already
gone (rare — would require two parallel `/check-inbox` runs on the same inbox),
skip and continue. Do not abort. This is idempotent by design.

## Step 4 — Summary

After processing all pending messages, print a one-line summary:

```
check-inbox: archived <N> message(s) for <AGENT>.
```

Post-condition: `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` contains zero `status: pending` files.
The `archive/` subdirectory is the only remaining populated location.

## Refusal rules

- If the agent directory `agents/<AGENT>/` does not exist, refuse:
  `check-inbox: unknown agent <name>`
- If `agents/<AGENT>/inbox/` does not exist, print:
  `check-inbox: inbox directory not found for <AGENT> — no messages`
  and exit 0 (not an error; the inbox may never have been written to).
- Never write secrets into any message body.
- Never modify any field other than `status` and adding `read_at`.
- Never write to `archive/` from the `send` path — the `send` path in
  `/agent-ops` always writes to the flat `inbox/` directory only.

## Duong — 2026-04-24T09:32:09Z

Base directory for this skill: /Users/duongntd99/Documents/Personal/strawberry-agents/.claude/skills/pre-compact-save

# /pre-compact-save — Pre-Compact Memory Consolidation

## When to use

- Before running `/compact` on an Evelynn or Sona coordinator session
- When the PreCompact hook blocks `/compact` and asks you to consolidate first
- When you want a mid-session snapshot without ending the session

## When NOT to use

- Subagent sessions (out of scope — Lissandra only handles coordinator sessions)
- Actual session end (use `/end-session` instead — it produces the full transcript archive)
- Immediately after a recent consolidation (redundant; worst case it produces a duplicate)

## Arguments

`` (optional): `evelynn` or `sona` to override auto-detection. Empty → auto-detect from session greeting.

## Protocol

1. **Preflight.**
   - Read the session jsonl path: `~/.claude/projects/<project-slug>/<session-id>.jsonl`. Derive `session_id` and `transcript_path` from the current environment.
   - If `` is non-empty, use it as the coordinator. Otherwise detect:
     - Scan the first 3 user messages for `Hey Sona` (case-insensitive) → coordinator = `sona`
     - Otherwise coordinator = `evelynn` (repo default per CLAUDE.md Caller Routing)
   - Cross-check `[concern: work]` vs `[concern: personal]` tags on subagent prompts. Contradiction → refuse with a diagnostic.

2. **Spawn Lissandra** via the Agent tool with `subagent_type: "Lissandra"`. Note: Lissandra updates `open-threads.md` and regenerates `INDEX.md` as part of the coordinator shard write, same as `/end-session` Step 6b. Prompt shape:

   ```
   [concern: <personal|work>]

   Consolidate this coordinator session before /compact. You are impersonating <coordinator>.

   - session_id: <uuid>
   - transcript_path: <absolute path to jsonl>
   - coordinator: <evelynn|sona>

   Run the full protocol in your agent definition (handoff shard, session shard, conditional learnings, journal entry, optional transcript excerpt, commit, sentinel). Write to `agents/<coordinator>/...` directories only. Use the coordinator's first-person voice.

   Report back with: artifact paths, commit SHA, push status, skipped steps (if any), warnings.
   ```

3. **Write coordinator identity hint file.**
   - Determine the coordinator name: use `$CLAUDE_AGENT_NAME` if set and valid (`evelynn`/`sona`); otherwise use the coordinator name resolved in step 1.
   - Write one lowercase line (`evelynn` or `sona`) to `.coordinator-identity` at repo root (`git rev-parse --show-toplevel`). This hint is consumed by `scripts/hooks/sessionstart-coordinator-identity.sh` on `claude --resume` to pin the correct coordinator identity when env vars are not available.
   - Example: `printf 'sona\n' > "$(git rev-parse --show-toplevel)/.coordinator-identity"`
   - The file is gitignored (per-checkout state, never committed).

4. **On Lissandra return:**
   - Verify the sentinel file exists at `/tmp/claude-precompact-saved-<session_id>`. If not, report failure and exit — the PreCompact hook will still block on next `/compact`.
   - Verify the commit landed on main. `git log -1 --format='%H %s'` should show Lissandra's consolidation commit.
   - Report the artifact paths + commit SHA back to the coordinator.

5. **Done.** Coordinator can now safely run `/compact`; the PreCompact hook will see the sentinel and allow compaction.

## Failure modes

- **Coordinator detection contradiction** — refuse, surface the inconsistency. Duong resolves manually by supplying ``.
- **Lissandra commit rejected by pre-push hook** — Lissandra reports verbatim. Do not retry; let Duong diagnose.
- **No sentinel after Lissandra return** — indicates Lissandra's final step didn't fire. Report and exit without touching the sentinel ourselves (the sentinel is Lissandra's signature that she completed).

## What this skill does NOT do

- Does not run `/end-session`. That skill is `disable-model-invocation: true` for a reason.
- Does not compact. You still run `/compact` yourself after this skill succeeds.
- Does not archive the full session transcript. That is end-session's job.
